# ASEAN, China and EM

## ASEAN: Order of merit
- Establishing a strategic framework for portfolio allocation across the region.

## Chasing China?
- We are unconvincied recent price action has longevely. Stay benchmark.

## The case for EM
- EM equities have underwhelmed versus DM. We see room for improvement.

# ASEAN: Order of merit

## Key decision points for ASEAN account

- 65% of index weight
- 57% of traded value
- Only 26% of MSCI constituents ($1 out of 182 stocks)

# ASEAN: Order of Merit

## YTD there has been a noticeable mismatch between markets' signalling and actual performance.

## Largest dollar ASEAN decisions exited from most to least preferred across forecast metrics.

# Indonesia (40% oversupply)

## Key Points

- **Funding Gap**: Indonesia's funding gap has dropped well below the level associated with output stability.
- **EV Industry**: The EV industry may rise to 1.5% of GDP.
- **Infrastructure**: Other manufacturing, infrastructure may rise to 1.5% of GDP.

# Singapore (Benchmark)

## Overview

# Malaysia (60% Undereweight)

## Key Insights

### 1. Oil Price and Net Energy Exports
- **Graph 1:**
  - **Title:** MSC Malaysia versus the oil price (with net energy exports)
  - **X-Axis:** Dates (Jan 01 to Mar 20)
  - **Y-Axis:** Oil energy exports (left) and GDP (right)
  - **Description:** The graph shows the relationship between oil prices and net energy exports for Malaysia. A higher oil price supports the ringgit, which in turn supports net energy exports.

- **Graph 2:**
  - **Title:** Malaysia BDFP funding gap versus USDMF monetization
  - **X-Axis:** Dates (Jan 01 to Mar 20)
  - **Y-Axis:** Funding gap (left) and USDMF monetization (right)
  - **Description:** The graph illustrates the funding gap between Malaysia BDFP and USDMF, highlighting the impact of MTP2 overruns.

### 2. External Position and NMY Weakness
- **Text:**
  - **Title:** The deterioration of Malaysia's external position is consistent with continued MNR weakness
  - **Description:** The text explains the relationship between Malaysia's external position and the weakness of the ringgit.

### 3. Footer
- **Logo:** CLSA
- **Source:**
  - **Title:** CLSA: MSC Malaysia: International Trade Center
  - **Description:** The source provides the data and information used in the graphs.

# Malaysia (60% underweight)

## Key Findings
- **ROE is 25%-30% inferior to EM while the price book discount to EM is only around 15%:**
  - The image highlights the underweight status of Malaysia, with a relative performance that is 25%-30% inferior to Emerging Markets (EM) while the price book discount to EM is 15%.

- **We see no relative improvement in relative value creation, which drives relative performance:**
  - The text emphasizes the lack of relative value creation, which is a key factor in driving the relative performance of Malaysia.

# Chasing China?

## 1. Uncertainty of Property Valuation

There is uncertainty of property valuation given official statistics show pricing down only 10%.

Policymakers may be cautious about current account erosion with rising consumption share.

# Chasing China?

## Key Points

- **There is also constraint on the magnitude of any fiscal stimulus given a 0.8% of GDP deficit.**
- **Public sector debt at 85% of GDP has risen by 45ppt over 10Y, more than any EM DM.**

## China Fiscal Outlook

| **China general government debt in GDP** | **China general government debt as % GDP** | **China general government debt as % GDP** |
|---------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------|
| 6%                                   | 2%                                       | 2%                                       |
| 5%                                   | 1%                                       | 1%                                       |
| 4%                                   | 0%                                       | 0%                                       |

# The case for EM

## Introduction

Since 2021 EM ex China has kept pace with Japan yet outperformed the S&P500 by 33%. In contrast with the tepid mood on EM, find an abundance of macro data points to replace.

# The Case for EM

## Across EM conditions are ripe for policymakers to begin easing, albeit waiting for the Fed cut.
EM real interest rates are at a 50bps positive spread over DM, or a lesser 30bps in China.

# The Case for EM

## Introduction

EM (Emerging Markets) equities can catch up with EM bonds which have been outperforming since July 2022. EM equities typically rally with a steepening global yield curve pre-launched via easing.

# The Case for EM

In May more than half of global PMI were in expansionary territory, the first time since 3Q22.

With the greatest concentration of surveys showing expansionary conditions in EM,

Global headline manufacturing PMI surveys above 50% (16).

Emerging markets (EM) has developed markets (G3) headline PMI and new orders.

# The Case for EM

## Introduction

The case for Emerging Markets (EM) is based on the 49% price-to-book discount, which has been the greatest in 23 years. EM offers 1.5x the dividend yield of DM equities at 2.8% versus 1.8%, respectively.

# The Case for EM

## Key Findings

- **Yet EM ex China foreign ownership at 29% remains at the lower end of the post-2007 history.**
- **Other than Brazil, Taiwan, Mexico & India foreign ownership is at the low end of the 1% range.**

## Foreign Ownership Series

# Important notices

## 2004/124 Limited CLEAR with U.S. Secretary of State and U.S. OVPs

### 1. Introduction

This document is a summary of the 2004/124 Limited CLEAR with U.S. Secretary of State and U.S. OVPs. It provides information on the purpose, scope, and requirements of the document.

### 2. Purpose

The purpose of this document is to provide information on the 2004/124 Limited CLEAR with U.S. Secretary of State and U.S. OVPs. It aims to inform users about the document's content, requirements, and any relevant updates.

### 3. Scope

This document is intended for use by individuals and organizations that are involved in the 2004/124 Limited CLEAR with U.S. Secretary of State and U.S. OVPs. It does not apply to other individuals or organizations.

### 4. Requirements

The 2004/124 Limited CLEAR with U.S. Secretary of State and U.S. OVPs requires users to provide certain information and documentation. This includes personal information, identification documents, and other relevant data.

### 5. Exemptions

Certain individuals and organizations may be exempt from the requirements of the 2004/124 Limited CLEAR with U.S. Secretary of State and U.S. OVPs. These exemptions are outlined in the document.

### 6. Contact Information

For any questions or concerns regarding the 2004/124 Limited CLEAR with U.S. Secretary of State and U.S. OVPs, users should contact the relevant authorities.

### 7. Conclusion

This document provides a summary of the 2004/124 Limited CLEAR with U.S. Secretary of State and U.S. OVPs. It aims to inform users about the document's content, requirements, and any relevant updates.
